   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Kiribati</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Country in the western Pacific Ocean
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the island nation. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Kiribati_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Kiribati (disambiguation)">Kiribati (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Kiritimati" title="Kiritimati">Kiritimati</a>, an island in the <a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a> and part of Kiribati.
      </div> 
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p>

         <td><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300">&nbsp;0.630<sup id="cite_ref-UNHDR_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHDR-8">[8]</a></sup><br><span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="color:orange">medium</span></span>&nbsp;·&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">134th</a></td>

         <th scope="row">Currency</th>

      </table> 
      <p><b>Kiribati</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ɪr/: 'irr' in 'mirror'">ɪr</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> officially the <b>Republic of Kiribati</b> (<a href="/wiki/Gilbertese_language" title="Gilbertese language">Gilbertese</a>: <i>[Ribaberiki] Kiribati</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-r1_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r1-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> is an <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independent</a> <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island nation</a> in the central <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. The permanent <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">population</a> is just over 110,000 (2015), more than half of whom live on <a href="/wiki/Tarawa" title="Tarawa">Tarawa atoll</a>. The state comprises <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Kiribati" title="List of islands of Kiribati">32 atolls</a> and one <a href="/wiki/Raised_coral_atoll" title="Raised coral atoll">raised coral island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banaba" title="Banaba">Banaba</a>. They have a total land area of 811 square kilometres (313 square miles)<sup id="cite_ref-IMF_2011_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_2011-12">[12]</a></sup> and are dispersed over 3.5&nbsp;million&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (1.4&nbsp;million&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). </p>
      <p>Their spread straddles the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a> and the <a href="/wiki/180th_meridian" title="180th meridian">180th meridian</a>, although the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a> goes round Kiribati and swings far to the east, almost reaching the <a href="/wiki/150th_meridian_west" title="150th meridian west">150°&nbsp;W meridian</a>. This brings Kiribati's easternmost islands, the southern <a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a> south of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, into the same day as the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a> and places them in the most advanced time zone on Earth: <a href="/wiki/UTC%2B14:00" title="UTC+14:00">UTC+14</a>. Kiribati is the only country in the world to be situated in all four <a href="/wiki/Hemispheres_of_Earth" title="Hemispheres of Earth">hemispheres</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kiribati gained its independence from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, becoming a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> in 1979. The capital, <a href="/wiki/South_Tarawa" title="South Tarawa">South Tarawa</a>, now the most populated area, consists of a number of islets, connected by a series of <a href="/wiki/Causeway" title="Causeway">causeways</a>. These comprise about half the area of <a href="/wiki/Tarawa" title="Tarawa">Tarawa</a> atoll. Previously the country had exported <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphate</a>; however, those mines are no longer viable with fisheries and export of <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">Copra</a> driving much of the economy. Kiribati is one of the least developed countries in the world and is highly dependent on international aid for its economy. </p>
      <p>Kiribati is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Community" title="Pacific Community">Pacific Community</a> (SPC), <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, and became a full member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 1999. As an island nation, the islands are <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change_on_island_nations" title="Effects of climate change on island nations">very vulnerable to climate change</a> and addressing climate change has been a central part of its international policy, as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Small_Island_States" title="Alliance of Small Island States">Alliance of Small Island States</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_pronunciation">Etymology and pronunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and pronunciation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The pronunciation differs: <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ɪr/: 'irr' in 'mirror'">ɪr</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <i>Kiribass</i> is the normal pronunciation as <i>-ti</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Gilbertese_language" title="Gilbertese language">Gilbertese language</a> represents an <i>s</i> sound. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:FMIB_53006_Gilbert_or_Kingsmill_Islands.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/FMIB_53006_Gilbert_or_Kingsmill_Islands.jpeg/220px-FMIB_53006_Gilbert_or_Kingsmill_Islands.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="340" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/FMIB_53006_Gilbert_or_Kingsmill_Islands.jpeg/330px-FMIB_53006_Gilbert_or_Kingsmill_Islands.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/FMIB_53006_Gilbert_or_Kingsmill_Islands.jpeg/440px-FMIB_53006_Gilbert_or_Kingsmill_Islands.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="490" data-file-height="758"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:FMIB_53006_Gilbert_or_Kingsmill_Islands.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of the Gilbert or Kingsmill Islands, 1890
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The name <i>Kiribati</i> was adopted in 1979 at independence. It is the <a href="/wiki/Gilbertese" class="mw-redirect" title="Gilbertese">Gilbertese</a> rendition of <i>Gilberts</i>, the plural of the English name of the nation's main archipelago, the <i>Gilbert Islands</i>. It was named <i>îles Gilbert</i> (French for <i>Gilbert Islands</i>) in about 1820 by Russian admiral <a href="/wiki/Adam_Johann_von_Krusenstern" title="Adam Johann von Krusenstern">Adam von Krusenstern</a><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> and French captain <a href="/wiki/Louis_Isidore_Duperrey" title="Louis Isidore Duperrey">Louis Duperrey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> after the British <a href="/wiki/Sea_captain" title="Sea captain">captain</a> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Gilbert_(sea_captain)" title="Thomas Gilbert (sea captain)">Thomas Gilbert</a>. Gilbert and captain <a href="/wiki/John_Marshall_(Royal_Navy_officer)" title="John Marshall (Royal Navy officer)">John Marshall</a> sighted some of the islands in 1788, while crossing the "outer passage" route from <a href="/wiki/Port_Jackson" title="Port Jackson">Port Jackson</a> to <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Canton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jps.auckland.ac.nz_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jps.auckland.ac.nz-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacdonald1982_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacdonald1982-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LifeMagazine1944-05-22_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LifeMagazine1944-05-22-18">[18]</a></sup> Both von Krusenstern's and Duperrey's maps, published in 1824, were written in French. In English, the archipelago, particularly the southern part, was often referred to as the Kingsmills in the 19th century, although the name Gilbert Islands was used increasingly, including in the <a href="/wiki/British_Western_Pacific_Territories" title="British Western Pacific Territories">Western Pacific Order in Council</a> of 1877 and in the Pacific Order of 1893.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The name Gilbert, already in the name of the British protectorate since 1892, was incorporated into the name of the entire <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_Colony" class="mw-redirect" title="Gilbert and Ellice Islands Colony">Gilbert and Ellice Islands Colony</a> (GIEC) from 1916 and was retained after the Ellice Islands became the separate nation of <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a> in 1976. The spelling of <i>Gilberts</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Gilbertese_language" title="Gilbertese language">Gilbertese language</a> as <i>Kiribati</i> may be found in books in Gilbertese prepared by missionaries, but with the meaning of Gilbertese (<a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">demonym</a> and language) (see e.g. Hawaiian Board of Missionaries, 1895).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHBM1895_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHBM1895-20">[20]</a></sup> The first mention as a dictionary entry of the word <i>Kiribati</i> as the native name of the country was written down in 1952 by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ernest_Sabatier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ernest Sabatier (page does not exist)">Ernest Sabatier</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernest_Sabatier" class="extiw" title="fr:Ernest Sabatier">fr</a>]</span> in his comprehensive <i>Dictionnaire gilbertin-français</i>. </p>
      <p>It is often suggested that the indigenous name for the Gilbert Islands proper is <i>Tungaru</i> (see e.g. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ernest_Sabatier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ernest Sabatier (page does not exist)">Ernest Sabatier</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernest_Sabatier" class="extiw" title="fr:Ernest Sabatier">fr</a>]</span>, 1952–1953, or <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Grimble" title="Arthur Grimble">Arthur Grimble</a>, 1989<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrimble1989_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrimble1989-21">[21]</a></sup>). However, the rendition Kiribati for Gilberts was chosen as the official name of the new independent nation by the Chief Minister, Sir <a href="/wiki/Ieremia_Tabai" title="Ieremia Tabai">Ieremia Tabai</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Kiribati" title="Cabinet of Kiribati">Cabinet</a>, on such grounds that it was modern,<sup id="cite_ref-cind_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cind-22">[22]</a></sup> and to comprehend the inclusion of outer islands (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands" title="Phoenix Islands">the Phoenix Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a>), which were not considered part of the Tungaru (or Gilberts) chain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESabatier1954_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESabatier1954-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[note 1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-25">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Kiribati" title="History of Kiribati">History of Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tabiteuean_warriors_of_the_Gilberts_Islands,_about_1840.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Tabiteuean_warriors_of_the_Gilberts_Islands%2C_about_1840.png/220px-Tabiteuean_warriors_of_the_Gilberts_Islands%2C_about_1840.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Tabiteuean_warriors_of_the_Gilberts_Islands%2C_about_1840.png/330px-Tabiteuean_warriors_of_the_Gilberts_Islands%2C_about_1840.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Tabiteuean_warriors_of_the_Gilberts_Islands%2C_about_1840.png/440px-Tabiteuean_warriors_of_the_Gilberts_Islands%2C_about_1840.png 2x" data-file-width="544" data-file-height="502"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The area now called Kiribati, mainly the 16 <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a>, has been inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian peoples</a> speaking the same <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_languages" title="Oceanic languages">Oceanic language</a>, from North to South, including the southernmost <a href="/wiki/Nui_(atoll)" title="Nui (atoll)">Nui</a>, since sometime between 3000 BC<sup id="cite_ref-cind_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cind-22">[22]</a></sup> and AD 1300.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas20035_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas20035-26">[25]</a></sup> The area was not completely isolated; later, settlers or voyagers from <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">Tonga</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> introduced some <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesian</a> cultural aspects, respectively. Intermarriage and intense navigation between the islands tended to blur cultural differences and resulted in a significant degree of cultural homogenisation.<sup id="cite_ref-brit_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-27">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> Local oral historians in the form of chiefly lore keepers suggest that the area was first inhabited by a group of seafaring people from <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesia</a>, who were described as being dark skinned, frizzy haired and short in stature. These <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a> were then visited by early <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian</a> seafarers from the west, a place called <i>Matang</i>, orally described as being tall and fair skinned. Eventually, both groups intermittently clashed and intermingled until they slowly became a uniform population. </p>
      <p>Around 1300 A.D, there was a mass exodus from <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a> at the same time that <a href="/wiki/Cannibalism" title="Cannibalism">cannibalism</a> was forcefully abolished there,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> leading to the addition of Polynesian ancestry into the mix of most Gilbertese people. These Samoans would later bring strong features of <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_languages" title="Polynesian languages">Polynesian languages</a> and culture, creating clans based on their own Samoan traditions and slowly intertwining with the indigenous clans and powers already dominant in Kiribati. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:KINGSMILL_IDOL.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/KINGSMILL_IDOL.png/220px-KINGSMILL_IDOL.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/KINGSMILL_IDOL.png/330px-KINGSMILL_IDOL.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/KINGSMILL_IDOL.png/440px-KINGSMILL_IDOL.png 2x" data-file-width="1774" data-file-height="1318"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:KINGSMILL_IDOL.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ceremonial <i>buoa</i>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1845</span>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Exploring_Expedition" title="United States Exploring Expedition">US Ex Ex</a>, from <i>Twenty Years Before the Mast</i>, by Charles Erskine
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Around the 15th century, with the stark contrasting systems of governance between the Northern Islands, primarily under chiefly rule (<i>uea</i>), and the Central and Southern Islands, primarily under the rule of their council of elders (<i>unimwaane</i>). <a href="/wiki/Tabiteuea" title="Tabiteuea">Tabiteuea</a> could be an exception as the sole island that is known as maintaining a traditional <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarian</a> society. The name Tabiteuea stems from the root phrase Tabu-te-Uea meaning "chiefs are forbidden".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Civil war soon became somehow a factor, with acquisition of land being the main form of conquest. Clans and chiefs began fighting over resources, fuelled by hatred and reignited blood feuds, which may have started months or decades before. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Makin_Islander.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Makin_Islander.jpg/200px-Makin_Islander.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Makin_Islander.jpg/300px-Makin_Islander.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Makin_Islander.jpg/400px-Makin_Islander.jpg 2x" data-file-width="591" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Makin_Islander.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Portrait of a native of the <a href="/wiki/Makin_(islands)" class="mw-redirect" title="Makin (islands)">Makin</a> islands, drawn by <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Thomas_Agate" title="Alfred Thomas Agate">Alfred Thomas Agate</a> (1841)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The turmoil lasted well into the European visitation and colonial era, which led to certain islands decimating their foes with the help of guns and cannon-equipped ships that some Europeans were coerced into using by the more cunning and persuasive among the I-Kiribati leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-jps.auckland.ac.nz_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jps.auckland.ac.nz-16">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The typical military arms of the I-Kiribati at this time were shark-tooth-embedded wooden spears, knives and swords, and garbs of armour fashioned from dense coconut fibre. They chiefly used these instead of the gunpowder and weapons of steel available at the time, because of the strong sentimental value of the equipment handed down through generations. Ranged weapons, such as bows, slings and javelins, were seldom used; <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Kiribati#Kiribati_traditional_martial_arts" title="Culture of Kiribati">hand-to-hand combat</a> was a prominent skill still practised today, though seldom mentioned because of various taboos associated with it, secrecy being the primary one. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Louis_Stevenson_Portrait_Vailima_Letters.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Robert_Louis_Stevenson_Portrait_Vailima_Letters.jpg/220px-Robert_Louis_Stevenson_Portrait_Vailima_Letters.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="332" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Robert_Louis_Stevenson_Portrait_Vailima_Letters.jpg/330px-Robert_Louis_Stevenson_Portrait_Vailima_Letters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Robert_Louis_Stevenson_Portrait_Vailima_Letters.jpg/440px-Robert_Louis_Stevenson_Portrait_Vailima_Letters.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2192" data-file-height="3303"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Louis_Stevenson_Portrait_Vailima_Letters.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Robert Louis Stevenson
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Abemama" title="Abemama">Abemama</a>'s High Chief <a href="/wiki/Tembinok%27" title="Tembinok'">Tembinok'</a> was the last of the dozens of expansionist Chiefs of <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a> of this period, despite Abemama historically conforming to the traditional Southern Island's governance of their respective "<i>unimwaane</i>". He was immortalised in <a href="/wiki/Robert_Louis_Stevenson" title="Robert Louis Stevenson">Robert Louis Stevenson</a>'s book <i>In the South Seas</i>, which delved into the High Chief's character and method of rule during Stevenson's stay in Abemama. The 90th anniversary of his arrival in the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a> was chosen to celebrate the independence of Kiribati on 12 July 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">Colonial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Colonial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/British_Western_Pacific_Territories" title="British Western Pacific Territories">British Western Pacific Territories</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands" title="Gilbert and Ellice Islands">Gilbert and Ellice Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tarawa_1873_map.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Tarawa_1873_map.jpg/220px-Tarawa_1873_map.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Tarawa_1873_map.jpg/330px-Tarawa_1873_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Tarawa_1873_map.jpg/440px-Tarawa_1873_map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4277" data-file-height="3473"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tarawa_1873_map.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Tarawa atoll, 1873
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>Chance visits by European ships occurred in the 17th and 18th centuries,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> while those ships attempted circumnavigations of the world, or sought sailing routes from the south to north Pacific Ocean. A passing trade, whaling the On-The-Line grounds,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> and labour ships associated with <a href="/wiki/Blackbirding" title="Blackbirding">blackbirding</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kanaka_(Pacific_Island_worker)" title="Kanaka (Pacific Island worker)">Kanakas</a> workers, visited the islands in large numbers during the 19th century, with social, economic, political, religious and cultural consequences. More than 9,000 workers were sent abroad from 1845 to 1895, most of them not returning.<sup id="cite_ref-cind_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cind-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The passing trade gave rise to European, Chinese, Samoan and other residents from the 1830s: they included <a href="/wiki/Beachcombing" title="Beachcombing">beachcombers</a>, castaways, traders and missionaries. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_a_protectorate_on_Abemama_by_Captain_Davis,_27th_May_1892.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Declaration_of_a_protectorate_on_Abemama_by_Captain_Davis%2C_27th_May_1892.JPG/220px-Declaration_of_a_protectorate_on_Abemama_by_Captain_Davis%2C_27th_May_1892.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Declaration_of_a_protectorate_on_Abemama_by_Captain_Davis%2C_27th_May_1892.JPG/330px-Declaration_of_a_protectorate_on_Abemama_by_Captain_Davis%2C_27th_May_1892.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Declaration_of_a_protectorate_on_Abemama_by_Captain_Davis%2C_27th_May_1892.JPG/440px-Declaration_of_a_protectorate_on_Abemama_by_Captain_Davis%2C_27th_May_1892.JPG 2x" data-file-width="538" data-file-height="332"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Declaration_of_a_protectorate_on_Abemama_by_Captain_Davis,_27th_May_1892.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Declaration of a protectorate on <a href="/wiki/Abemama" title="Abemama">Abemama</a> by Captain <a href="/wiki/Edward_H.M._Davis" title="Edward H.M. Davis">EHM Davis</a>, 27 May 1892
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1886, an <a href="/wiki/Anglo-German_Declarations_about_the_Western_Pacific_Ocean" title="Anglo-German Declarations about the Western Pacific Ocean">Anglo-German agreement</a> partitioned the "unclaimed" central Pacific, leaving <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a> in the German sphere of influence, while <a href="/wiki/Banaba" title="Banaba">Ocean Island</a> and the future GEIC wound up in the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British sphere of influence</a>. In 1892, local Gilbertese authorities (an <i>uea</i>, a chief from the Northern Gilbert Group, and <i>atun te boti</i> or head of clan<sup id="cite_ref-maude_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maude-36">[35]</a></sup>) on each of the Gilbert Islands agreed to Captain <a href="/wiki/Edward_H.M._Davis" title="Edward H.M. Davis">E.H.M. Davis</a> commanding <a href="/wiki/HMS_Royalist_(1883)" title="HMS Royalist (1883)">HMS <i>Royalist</i></a> of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> declaring them part of a <a href="/wiki/British_protectorate" title="British protectorate">British protectorate</a>, along with the nearby <a href="/wiki/Ellice_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Ellice Islands">Ellice Islands</a>. They were administered by a <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_the_Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands" title="Governor of the Gilbert and Ellice Islands">resident commissioner</a> based first on <a href="/wiki/Butaritari" title="Butaritari">Makin Islands</a> (1893–95), then in <a href="/wiki/Betio" title="Betio">Betio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tarawa" title="Tarawa">Tarawa</a> (1896–1908) and <a href="/wiki/Banaba" title="Banaba">Ocean Island</a> (1908–1942), protectorate who was under the <a href="/wiki/High_Commissioner_for_the_Western_Pacific" title="High Commissioner for the Western Pacific">Western Pacific High Commission</a> based in Fiji.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCtimeline_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCtimeline-37">[36]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Banaba" title="Banaba">Banaba</a>, known to Europeans as Ocean Island, was added to the protectorate in 1900, because of the <a href="/wiki/Phosphorite" title="Phosphorite">phosphate rock</a> of its soil (discovered in 1900). This <a href="/wiki/Phosphate_mining_in_Banaba_and_Nauru" title="Phosphate mining in Banaba and Nauru">discovery and the mining</a> ended the contracting of <a href="/wiki/Kanaka_(Pacific_Island_worker)" title="Kanaka (Pacific Island worker)">Kanakas workers</a> to farm plantations in <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">German Samoa</a> or Central America, with all the needed workers being used in Ocean Island extraction. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_1911_(Mar.)_Pandanus_Pine_1d._carmine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_1911_%28Mar.%29_Pandanus_Pine_1d._carmine.jpg/220px-Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_1911_%28Mar.%29_Pandanus_Pine_1d._carmine.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="265" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b8/Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_1911_%28Mar.%29_Pandanus_Pine_1d._carmine.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="247" data-file-height="297"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_1911_(Mar.)_Pandanus_Pine_1d._carmine.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>1911 stamp of the Gilbert and Ellice Islands protectorate, representing a <i><a href="/wiki/Pandanus_tectorius" title="Pandanus tectorius">Pandanus tectorius</a></i> tree.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The conduct of <a href="/wiki/William_Telfer_Campbell" title="William Telfer Campbell">William Telfer Campbell</a>, the second resident commissioner of the Gilberts and Ellice Islands of 1896 to 1908, was criticised as to his legislative, judicial and administrative management (including allegations of forced labour exacted from islanders) and became the subject of the 1909 report by Arthur Mahaffy.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> In 1913, an anonymous correspondent to <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Age" title="The New Age">The New Age</a></i> newspaper described the maladministration of W. Telfer Campbell and questioned the partiality of Arthur Mahaffy, because he was a former colonial official in the Gilberts.<sup id="cite_ref-AN_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AN-39">[38]</a></sup> The anonymous correspondent also criticised the operations of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Phosphate_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Phosphate Company">Pacific Phosphate Company</a> on Ocean Island.<sup id="cite_ref-AN_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AN-39">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_314_Clipper_in_cruise.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Boeing_314_Clipper_in_cruise.jpg/220px-Boeing_314_Clipper_in_cruise.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Boeing_314_Clipper_in_cruise.jpg/330px-Boeing_314_Clipper_in_cruise.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Boeing_314_Clipper_in_cruise.jpg/440px-Boeing_314_Clipper_in_cruise.jpg 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="310"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_314_Clipper_in_cruise.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Boeing_314_Clipper" title="Boeing 314 Clipper">Boeing 314 Clipper</a> in cruise, 1940
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The islands became the <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">crown colony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands" title="Gilbert and Ellice Islands">Gilbert and Ellice Islands</a> in 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-brit_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-27">[26]</a></sup> The Northern <a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a>, including Christmas Island (<a href="/wiki/Kiritimati" title="Kiritimati">Kiritimati</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> were added to the colony in 1919, and the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands" title="Phoenix Islands">Phoenix Islands</a> were added in 1937 with the purpose of a <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands_Settlement_Scheme" title="Phoenix Islands Settlement Scheme">Phoenix Islands Settlement Scheme</a>. On 12 July 1940, <a href="/wiki/Pan_Am" title="Pan Am">Pan Am</a> Airways' <i><a href="/wiki/Boeing_314_Clipper" title="Boeing 314 Clipper">American Clipper</a></i> landed at <a href="/wiki/Kanton_Island" title="Kanton Island">Canton Island</a> for the first time during a flight from <a href="/wiki/Honolulu" title="Honolulu">Honolulu</a> to <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_(1937%E2%80%931976).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Flag_of_the_Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_%281937%E2%80%931976%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_%281937%E2%80%931976%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Flag_of_the_Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_%281937%E2%80%931976%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_%281937%E2%80%931976%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Flag_of_the_Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_%281937%E2%80%931976%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_%281937%E2%80%931976%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_(1937%E2%80%931976).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>1937 Colonial flag of <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands" title="Gilbert and Ellice Islands">Gilbert and Ellice Islands</a>. Its badge was drawn by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Grimble" title="Arthur Grimble">Arthur Grimble</a> in 1931.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sir <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Grimble" title="Arthur Grimble">Arthur Grimble</a> was a cadet administrative officer based at <a href="/wiki/Tarawa" title="Tarawa">Tarawa</a> (1913–1919) and became Resident Commissioner of the Gilbert and Ellice Islands colony in 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrimble1952_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrimble1952-42">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stamp_Gilbert_Ellice_Islands_1939_3p.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Stamp_Gilbert_Ellice_Islands_1939_3p.jpg/220px-Stamp_Gilbert_Ellice_Islands_1939_3p.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Stamp_Gilbert_Ellice_Islands_1939_3p.jpg/330px-Stamp_Gilbert_Ellice_Islands_1939_3p.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Stamp_Gilbert_Ellice_Islands_1939_3p.jpg/440px-Stamp_Gilbert_Ellice_Islands_1939_3p.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="675"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stamp_Gilbert_Ellice_Islands_1939_3p.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Stamp with portrait of <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">King George VI</a>, 1939
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1902, the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Cable_Station" title="Pacific Cable Station">Pacific Cable Board</a> laid the first trans-Pacific telegraph cable from <a href="/wiki/Bamfield" title="Bamfield">Bamfield</a>, British Columbia to <a href="/wiki/Fanning_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Fanning Island">Fanning Island</a> (Tabuaeran) in the Line Islands, and from Fiji to Fanning Island, thus completing the <a href="/wiki/All_Red_Line" title="All Red Line">All Red Line</a>, a series of telegraph lines circumnavigating the globe completely within the British Empire. The location of Fanning Island, one of the closest formations to Hawaii, led to its annexation by the British Empire in 1888. Nearby candidates including <a href="/wiki/Palmyra_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Palmyra Island">Palmyra Island</a> were not favoured due to the lack of adequate landing sites. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:165th_Infantry_assault_wave_attacking_Butaritari,_Yellow_Beach_Two,_find_it_slow_going_in_the_coral_bottom_waters...._-_NARA_-_531172.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/165th_Infantry_assault_wave_attacking_Butaritari%2C_Yellow_Beach_Two%2C_find_it_slow_going_in_the_coral_bottom_waters...._-_NARA_-_531172.tif/lossy-page1-220px-165th_Infantry_assault_wave_attacking_Butaritari%2C_Yellow_Beach_Two%2C_find_it_slow_going_in_the_coral_bottom_waters...._-_NARA_-_531172.tif.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/165th_Infantry_assault_wave_attacking_Butaritari%2C_Yellow_Beach_Two%2C_find_it_slow_going_in_the_coral_bottom_waters...._-_NARA_-_531172.tif/lossy-page1-330px-165th_Infantry_assault_wave_attacking_Butaritari%2C_Yellow_Beach_Two%2C_find_it_slow_going_in_the_coral_bottom_waters...._-_NARA_-_531172.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/165th_Infantry_assault_wave_attacking_Butaritari%2C_Yellow_Beach_Two%2C_find_it_slow_going_in_the_coral_bottom_waters...._-_NARA_-_531172.tif/lossy-page1-440px-165th_Infantry_assault_wave_attacking_Butaritari%2C_Yellow_Beach_Two%2C_find_it_slow_going_in_the_coral_bottom_waters...._-_NARA_-_531172.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2376"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:165th_Infantry_assault_wave_attacking_Butaritari,_Yellow_Beach_Two,_find_it_slow_going_in_the_coral_bottom_waters...._-_NARA_-_531172.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>165th Infantry assault wave attacking Butaritari, Yellow Beach Two, <a href="/wiki/Butaritari" title="Butaritari">Makin atoll</a>, 20 November 1943
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The United States eventually incorporated the Northern <a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a> into its territories, and did the same with the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands" title="Phoenix Islands">Phoenix Islands</a>, which lie between Gilberts and the Line Islands, including <a href="/wiki/Howland_Island" title="Howland Island">Howland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jarvis_Island" title="Jarvis Island">Jarvis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Baker_Island" title="Baker Island">Baker</a> islands, thus causing a territorial dispute. That was eventually resolved and they finally became part of Kiribati under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tarawa" title="Treaty of Tarawa">Treaty of Tarawa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tarawa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Tarawa.jpg/220px-Tarawa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Tarawa.jpg/330px-Tarawa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Tarawa.jpg/440px-Tarawa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2370"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tarawa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>American Marines assault a Japanese bunker during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tarawa" title="Battle of Tarawa">Battle of Tarawa</a>, November 1943.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a>, during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Butaritari" title="Butaritari">Butaritari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tarawa" title="Tarawa">Tarawa</a>, and others of the Northern Gilbert group, were <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_the_Gilbert_Islands" title="Japanese occupation of the Gilbert Islands">occupied by Japan</a> from 1941 to 1943. <a href="/wiki/Betio" title="Betio">Betio</a> became an airfield and supply base. The expulsion of the Japanese military in late 1943 involved one of the bloodiest battles in <a href="/wiki/US_Marine_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="US Marine Corps">US Marine Corps</a> history. Marines landed in November 1943 and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tarawa" title="Battle of Tarawa">Battle of Tarawa</a> ensued. <a href="/wiki/Banaba" title="Banaba">Ocean Island</a>, where were the headquarters of the colony, was bombed, evacuated and occupied by Japan in 1942 and only freed in 1945, after the massacre of all but one Banabans by the Japanese forces. <a href="/wiki/Funafuti" title="Funafuti">Funafuti</a> hosted then the provisional headquarters of the colony from 1942 to 1946, when <a href="/wiki/Tarawa" title="Tarawa">Tarawa</a> returned to host the headquarters, replacing Ocean Island. </p>
      <p>At the end of 1945, most of the remaining inhabitants of <a href="/wiki/Banaba" title="Banaba">Banaba</a>, repatriated from <a href="/wiki/Kosrae" title="Kosrae">Kosrae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tarawa" title="Tarawa">Tarawa</a>, were relocated to <a href="/wiki/Rabi_Island" title="Rabi Island">Rabi Island</a>, a land of Fiji that the British government had acquired in 1942 for this purpose.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 1 January 1953, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_resident_commissioners_and_governors_of_the_Solomon_Islands" title="List of resident commissioners and governors of the Solomon Islands">British governor</a> of the colony was transferred in the new capital of <a href="/wiki/Honiara" title="Honiara">Honiara</a>, to the <a href="/wiki/British_Solomon_Islands" title="British Solomon Islands">British Solomon Islands</a>, with the Gilberts' Resident Commissioner still headquartered in Tarawa. </p>
      <p>Further military operations in the colony occurred in the late 1950s and early 1960s when <a href="/wiki/Kiritimati" title="Kiritimati">Christmas Island</a> was used by the United States and United Kingdom for <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_testing" title="Nuclear weapons testing">nuclear weapons testing</a> including <a href="/wiki/Thermonuclear_weapon" title="Thermonuclear weapon">hydrogen bombs</a>. </p>
      <p>Institutions of internal self-rule were established on Tarawa from about 1967. The Ellice Islands asked for separation from the rest of the colony in 1974 and granted their own internal self-rule institutions. The separation entered into force on 1 January 1976. In 1978, the Ellice Islands became the independent nation of <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-25">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:KiribatiPresidential_Residence.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/KiribatiPresidential_Residence.jpg/220px-KiribatiPresidential_Residence.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/KiribatiPresidential_Residence.jpg/330px-KiribatiPresidential_Residence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/KiribatiPresidential_Residence.jpg/440px-KiribatiPresidential_Residence.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:KiribatiPresidential_Residence.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Presidential residence, former <a href="/wiki/Government_House" title="Government House">Government House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bairiki" title="Bairiki">Bairiki</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Gilbert Islands gained independence as the Republic of Kiribati on 12 July 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Then, in September, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> relinquished all claims to the sparsely inhabited <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands" title="Phoenix Islands">Phoenix</a> and <a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a>, in a 1979 treaty of friendship with Kiribati (<a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tarawa" title="Treaty of Tarawa">ratified in 1983</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Gilbertese_language" title="Gilbertese language">Gilbertese</a> name for the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a> proper is "Tungaru", the new state chose the name "Kiribati", the Gilbertese spelling of "Gilberts", because it was more modern and as an equivalent of the former colony to acknowledge the inclusion of <a href="/wiki/Banaba" title="Banaba">Banaba</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands" title="Phoenix Islands">Phoenix Islands</a>. The last two archipelagoes were never initially occupied by Gilbertese until the British authorities, and later the Republic Government, resettled Gilbertese there under resettlement schemes.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-25">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-47">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1982, the first <a href="/wiki/1982_Kiribati_parliamentary_election" title="1982 Kiribati parliamentary election">elections since independence</a> were held. A no confidence vote provoked the <a href="/wiki/1983_Kiribati_parliamentary_election" title="1983 Kiribati parliamentary election">1983 new election</a>. </p>
      <p>In the post-independence era, <a href="/wiki/Overcrowding" title="Overcrowding">overcrowding</a> has been an issue, at least in British and aid organisations' eyes. In 1988, an announcement was made that 4,700 residents of the main island group would be resettled onto less-populated islands. </p>
      <p>In September 1994, <a href="/wiki/Teburoro_Tito" title="Teburoro Tito">Teburoro Tito</a> from the opposition was elected president. </p>
      <p>In 1995, Kiribati unilaterally moved the <a href="/wiki/International_date_line" class="mw-redirect" title="International date line">international date line</a> far to the east to encompass the Line Islands group, so that the nation would no longer be divided by the date line. The move, which fulfilled one of President Tito's campaign promises, was intended to allow businesses across the expansive nation to keep the same business week. This also enabled Kiribati to become the first country to see the dawn of the <a href="/wiki/Third_millennium" class="mw-redirect" title="Third millennium">third millennium</a>, an event of significance for tourism. Tito was re-elected in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1999, Kiribati became a full member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, 20 years after independence. </p>
      <p>In 2002, Kiribati passed a controversial law that enabled the government to shut down newspaper publishers. The legislation followed the launching of Kiribati's first successful non-government-run newspaper. President Tito was re-elected in 2003 but was removed from office in March 2003 by a no-confidence vote and replaced by a Council of State. <a href="/wiki/Anote_Tong" title="Anote Tong">Anote Tong</a> of the opposition party <a href="/wiki/Boutokaan_Te_Koaua" class="mw-redirect" title="Boutokaan Te Koaua">Boutokaan Te Koaua</a> was elected to succeed Tito in July 2003. He was re-elected in 2007 and in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:185px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:President_Anote_Tong.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/90/President_Anote_Tong.jpg" decoding="async" width="183" height="234" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="183" data-file-height="234"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:President_Anote_Tong.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Anote Tong
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><br> In June 2008, Kiribati officials asked Australia and New Zealand to accept Kiribati citizens as permanent refugees. </p>
      <p>Kiribati is expected to be the first country to lose all its land territory to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>. In June 2008, the Kiribati President Anote Tong said that the country had reached "the point of no return." He added, "To plan for the day when you no longer have a country is indeed painful but I think we have to do that."<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In January 2012, Anote Tong was re-elected for a third and last successive term. In early 2012, the government of Kiribati purchased the 2,200-hectare Natoavatu Estate on the second largest island of Fiji, <a href="/wiki/Vanua_Levu" title="Vanua Levu">Vanua Levu</a>. At the time it was widely reported<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> that the government planned to evacuate the entire population of Kiribati to Fiji. In April 2013, President Tong began urging citizens to evacuate the islands and migrate elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> In May 2014, the Office of the President confirmed the purchase of some 5,460 acres of land on Vanua Levu at a cost of 9.3 million Australian dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Kiribati" title="Politics of Kiribati">Politics of Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:KiribatiParliamentHouse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/KiribatiParliamentHouse.jpg/220px-KiribatiParliamentHouse.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/KiribatiParliamentHouse.jpg/330px-KiribatiParliamentHouse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/KiribatiParliamentHouse.jpg/440px-KiribatiParliamentHouse.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:KiribatiParliamentHouse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Maneaba" title="Maneaba">Maneaba</a> ni Maungatabu, House of Assembly, 2000.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Kiribati" title="Constitution of Kiribati">Constitution of Kiribati</a>, promulgated 12 July 1979, provides for free and open elections in a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>. </p>
      <p>The executive branch consists of a <a href="/wiki/President_of_Kiribati" title="President of Kiribati">president</a> (<i>te Beretitenti</i>), a <a href="/wiki/Vice-President_of_Kiribati" title="Vice-President of Kiribati">vice-president</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Kiribati" title="Cabinet of Kiribati">cabinet</a>. The president, who is also chief of the cabinet, is directly elected by the citizens, after the legislature nominates three or four persons from among its members to be candidates in the ensuing presidential election. The president is limited in the terms they can serve for to three four-year terms. He remains a member of the Assembly while serving as president. The cabinet is composed of the president, vice-president, and 13 ministers (appointed by the president) who are also <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_(Kiribati)" title="House of Assembly (Kiribati)">MPs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-US_State_Dept_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_State_Dept-59">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribati_House_of_Assembly.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Kiribati_House_of_Assembly.jpg/220px-Kiribati_House_of_Assembly.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Kiribati_House_of_Assembly.jpg/330px-Kiribati_House_of_Assembly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Kiribati_House_of_Assembly.jpg/440px-Kiribati_House_of_Assembly.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1765" data-file-height="1185"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribati_House_of_Assembly.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Old House of Assembly (1974-2000)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The legislative branch is the unicameral <i><a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_(Kiribati)" title="House of Assembly (Kiribati)">Maneaba ni Maungatabu</a></i> (House of Assembly). Its members are elected, including by constitutional mandate, a nominated representative of the Banaban people in <a href="/wiki/Rabi_Island" title="Rabi Island">Rabi Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> (<a href="/wiki/Banaba" title="Banaba">Banaba</a>, former Ocean Island), in addition to, until 2016, the attorney general, who served as an <i>ex officio</i> member from 1979 to 2016. Legislators serve for a four-year term. </p>
      <p>The constitutional provisions governing administration of justice are similar to those in other former British possessions in that the judiciary is free from governmental interference. The judicial branch is made up of the High Court (in Betio) and the Court of Appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-US_State_Dept_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_State_Dept-59">[58]</a></sup> The president appoints the presiding judges. </p>
      <p>Local government is through island councils with elected members. Local affairs are handled in a manner similar to town meetings in colonial America. Island councils make their own estimates of revenue and expenditure<sup id="cite_ref-US_State_Dept_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_State_Dept-59">[58]</a></sup> and generally are free from central government controls. There are a total of 21 inhabited islands in Kiribati. Each inhabited island has its own council. Since independence, Kiribati is no longer divided into districts (see <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Kiribati" class="mw-redirect" title="Districts of Kiribati">Subdivisions of Kiribati</a>). </p>
      <p>Kiribati has formal political parties but their organisation is quite informal.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> Ad&nbsp;hoc opposition groups tend to coalesce around specific issues. There is universal suffrage at age 18.<sup id="cite_ref-US_State_Dept_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_State_Dept-59">[58]</a></sup> Today the only recognisable parties are the <a href="/wiki/Boutokaan_Kiribati_Moa_Party" title="Boutokaan Kiribati Moa Party">Boutokaan Kiribati Moa Party</a>, former <i>Boutokaan te Koaua</i>, and <a href="/wiki/Tobwaan_Kiribati_Party" title="Tobwaan Kiribati Party">Tobwaan Kiribati Party</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Kiribati" title="Foreign relations of Kiribati">Foreign relations of Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kiribati maintains close relations with its Pacific neighbours, Australia, New Zealand, Japan and Fiji. The first three of these provide the bulk of the country's foreign aid. <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> and Japan also have specified-period licences to fish in Kiribati's waters.<sup id="cite_ref-US_State_Dept_59-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_State_Dept-59">[58]</a></sup> There were three resident diplomatic missions headquartered in Kiribati: the Embassies of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> (Taiwan) until 2019, replaced by China in 2020 and the High Commissions of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Australian_High_Commissioners_to_Kiribati" title="List of Australian High Commissioners to Kiribati">Australia</a> and New Zealand.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2020)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In November 1999 Kiribati agreed to allow Japan's <a href="/wiki/National_Space_Development_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="National Space Development Agency">National Space Development Agency</a> to lease land on <a href="/wiki/Kiritimati" title="Kiritimati">Christmas Island</a> for 20 years, on which to build a <a href="/wiki/Spaceport" title="Spaceport">spaceport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SpaceDaily2000_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpaceDaily2000-61">[60]</a></sup> The agreement stipulated that Japan was to pay US$840,000 per year and would also pay for any damage to roads and the environment.<sup id="cite_ref-SpaceDaily2000_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpaceDaily2000-61">[60]</a></sup> A Japanese-built downrange <a href="/wiki/Tracking_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Tracking station">tracking station</a> operates on Kiritimati<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> and an abandoned airfield on the island was designated as the landing strip for a proposed reusable unmanned <a href="/wiki/Space_shuttle" class="mw-redirect" title="Space shuttle">space shuttle</a> called <a href="/wiki/HOPE-X" title="HOPE-X">HOPE-X</a>. HOPE-X, however, was eventually cancelled by Japan in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a
