decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/%E4%BA%94%E6%9C%88%E4%BA%8C%E5%8D%81%E4%B8%89%E6%97%A5%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%8E%A5%E8%A6%8B%E5%90%89%E9%87%8C%E5%B7%B4%E6%96%AF%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E9%A6%AC%E8%8C%82%28Taneti_Maamau%29%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E4%B9%99%E8%A1%8C_%2827208262585%29.jpg/330px-%E4%BA%94%E6%9C%88%E4%BA%8C%E5%8D%81%E4%B8%89%E6%97%A5%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%8E%A5%E8%A6%8B%E5%90%89%E9%87%8C%E5%B7%B4%E6%96%AF%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E9%A6%AC%E8%8C%82%28Taneti_Maamau%29%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E4%B9%99%E8%A1%8C_%2827208262585%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/%E4%BA%94%E6%9C%88%E4%BA%8C%E5%8D%81%E4%B8%89%E6%97%A5%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%8E%A5%E8%A6%8B%E5%90%89%E9%87%8C%E5%B7%B4%E6%96%AF%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E9%A6%AC%E8%8C%82%28Taneti_Maamau%29%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E4%B9%99%E8%A1%8C_%2827208262585%29.jpg/440px-%E4%BA%94%E6%9C%88%E4%BA%8C%E5%8D%81%E4%B8%89%E6%97%A5%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%8E%A5%E8%A6%8B%E5%90%89%E9%87%8C%E5%B7%B4%E6%96%AF%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E9%A6%AC%E8%8C%82%28Taneti_Maamau%29%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E4%B9%99%E8%A1%8C_%2827208262585%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4517" data-file-height="3011"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%E4%BA%94%E6%9C%88%E4%BA%8C%E5%8D%81%E4%B8%89%E6%97%A5%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E6%8E%A5%E8%A6%8B%E5%90%89%E9%87%8C%E5%B7%B4%E6%96%AF%E7%B8%BD%E7%B5%B1%E9%A6%AC%E8%8C%82(Taneti_Maamau)%E4%BC%89%E5%84%B7%E4%B9%99%E8%A1%8C_(27208262585).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kiribati President <a href="/wiki/Taneti_Maamau" title="Taneti Maamau">Taneti Maamau</a> meets with Taiwanese President <a href="/wiki/Tsai_Ing-wen" title="Tsai Ing-wen">Tsai Ing-wen</a> on 23 May 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As one of the world's most vulnerable nations to the <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Effects of global warming">effects of global warming</a>, Kiribati has been an active participant in international diplomatic efforts relating to climate change, most importantly the <a href="/wiki/UNFCCC" class="mw-redirect" title="UNFCCC">UNFCCC</a> conferences of the parties (COP). Kiribati is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Small_Island_States" title="Alliance of Small Island States">Alliance of Small Island States</a> (AOSIS), an intergovernmental organisation of low-lying coastal and small island countries. Established in 1990, the main purpose of the alliance is to consolidate the voices of <a href="/wiki/Small_Island_Developing_States" title="Small Island Developing States">Small Island Developing States</a> (SIDS) to address global warming. AOSIS has been very active from its inception, putting forward the first draft text in the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> negotiations as early as 1994. </p>
      <p>In 2009, President Tong attended the <a href="/wiki/Climate_Vulnerable_Forum" title="Climate Vulnerable Forum">Climate Vulnerable Forum</a> (<a href="/wiki/Climate_Vulnerable_Forum" title="Climate Vulnerable Forum">V11</a>) in the <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a>, with 10 other countries that are <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_vulnerability" title="Climate change vulnerability">vulnerable to climate change</a>, and signed the Bandos Island declaration on 10 November 2009, pledging to show moral leadership and commence greening their economies by voluntarily committing to achieving <a href="/wiki/Carbon_neutrality" title="Carbon neutrality">carbon neutrality</a>. </p>
      <p>In November 2010, Kiribati hosted the <a href="/wiki/Tarawa_Climate_Change_Conference" title="Tarawa Climate Change Conference">Tarawa Climate Change Conference</a> (TCCC) to support the president of Kiribati's initiative to hold a consultative forum between vulnerable states and their partners. The conference strove to create an enabling environment for multi-party negotiations under the auspices of the UNFCCC. The conference was a successor event to the Climate Vulnerable Forum.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> The ultimate objective of TCCC was to reduce the number and intensity of fault lines between parties to the COP process, explore elements of agreement between the parties and thereby to support Kiribati's and other parties' contribution to <a href="/wiki/COP16" class="mw-redirect" title="COP16">COP16</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Cancun" class="mw-redirect" title="Cancun">Cancun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, from 29 November to 10 December 2010. </p>
      <p>In 2013, President Tong spoke of climate-change induced <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a> as "inevitable". "For our people to survive, then they will have to migrate. Either we can wait for the time when we have to move people en masse or we can prepare them—beginning from now ..."<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> In New York in 2014, per <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i>, President Tong told <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> that "according to the projections, within this century, the water will be higher than the highest point in our lands".<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> In 2014, President Tong finalised the purchase of a 20&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (7.7&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) stretch of land on Vanua Levu, one of the larger Fiji islands, 2,000&nbsp;km away. A move described by Tong as an "absolute necessity" should the nation be completely submerged under water.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2013 attention was drawn to a claim of a Kiribati man of being a <a href="/wiki/Environmental_migrant#In_Asia_&amp;_the_Pacific" title="Environmental migrant">"climate change refugee"</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Convention_relating_to_the_Status_of_Refugees" class="mw-redirect" title="Convention relating to the Status of Refugees">Convention relating to the Status of Refugees</a> (1951).<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC-68">[67]</a></sup> However this claim was determined by the New Zealand High Court to be untenable.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> The New Zealand Court of Appeal also rejected the claim in a <a href="/wiki/Teitiota_v_Chief_Executive_Ministry_of_Business,_Innovation_and_Employment" title="Teitiota v Chief Executive Ministry of Business, Innovation and Employment">2014 decision</a>. On further appeal the New Zealand Supreme Court confirmed the earlier adverse rulings against the application for refugee status, but rejected the proposition "that environmental degradation resulting from climate change or other natural disasters could never create a pathway into the Refugee Convention or protected person jurisdiction".<sup id="cite_ref-TSC_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TSC-70">[69]</a></sup> In 2017, Kiribati signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 20 September 2019, the government of Kiribati restored its diplomatic relationship with the People's Republic of China and simultaneously stopped its diplomatic relationship with Taiwan.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> offered a 737 aircraft and ferries to Kiribati for the decision, according to Taiwan's foreign minister, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Wu" title="Joseph Wu">Joseph Wu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement_and_military">Law enforcement and military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Law enforcement and military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:RKS_Teanoai,_during_a_joint_exercise_2019-11-07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/RKS_Teanoai%2C_during_a_joint_exercise_2019-11-07.jpg/220px-RKS_Teanoai%2C_during_a_joint_exercise_2019-11-07.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/RKS_Teanoai%2C_during_a_joint_exercise_2019-11-07.jpg/330px-RKS_Teanoai%2C_during_a_joint_exercise_2019-11-07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8e/RKS_Teanoai%2C_during_a_joint_exercise_2019-11-07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="359" data-file-height="307"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:RKS_Teanoai,_during_a_joint_exercise_2019-11-07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Police vessel RKS <i>Teanoai</i>, in 2019.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Kiribati" title="Law enforcement in Kiribati">Law enforcement in Kiribati</a> is carried out by the Kiribati Police Service which is responsible for all law enforcement and paramilitary duties for the island nation. There are police posts located on all of the islands. The police have one patrol boat, the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-class" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific-class">Pacific-class</a> patrol boat <a href="/wiki/RKS_Teanoai_(301)" title="RKS Teanoai (301)">RKS <i>Teanoai</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> Kiribati has no military and relies on both <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> for its defence. </p>
      <p>The main prison in Kiribati is located in <a href="/wiki/Betio" title="Betio">Betio</a>, named the Walter Betio Prison. There is also a prison in <a href="/wiki/London,_Kiribati" title="London, Kiribati">London</a> on <a href="/wiki/Kiritimati" title="Kiritimati">Kiritimati</a>. </p>
      <p>Male <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Kiribati" title="LGBT rights in Kiribati">homosexuality</a> is illegal in Kiribati, with a penalty up to 14 years in prison, according to a historical British law, but this law is not enforced. Kiribati has not yet followed the lead of the United Kingdom, following its <a href="/wiki/Wolfenden_report" title="Wolfenden report">Wolfenden report</a>, to decriminalise acts of male homosexuality, beginning with provisions in the UK's Sexual Offences Act 1957. Female homosexuality is legal, but lesbians may face violence and discrimination. However, employment discrimination on the basis of sexual orientation is prohibited.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CarolinePic-Kepler-Long.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/CarolinePic-Kepler-Long.JPG/220px-CarolinePic-Kepler-Long.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/CarolinePic-Kepler-Long.JPG/330px-CarolinePic-Kepler-Long.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/CarolinePic-Kepler-Long.JPG/440px-CarolinePic-Kepler-Long.JPG 2x" data-file-width="495" data-file-height="331"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CarolinePic-Kepler-Long.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a>: <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Island" title="Caroline Island">Caroline Island</a> channel between west side of Long Island and Nake Island.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Marakei_Atoll.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Marakei_Atoll.jpg/220px-Marakei_Atoll.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Marakei_Atoll.jpg/330px-Marakei_Atoll.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Marakei_Atoll.jpg/440px-Marakei_Atoll.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3060" data-file-height="2033"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Marakei_Atoll.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Marakei" title="Marakei">Marakei</a>, North Gilbert Islands
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Kiribati" class="mw-redirect" title="Districts of Kiribati">Districts of Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are 21 inhabited islands in Kiribati. Kiribati is divided geographically into three island groups, including a group that unites the <a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands" title="Phoenix Islands">Phoenix Islands</a> (ministry at <a href="/wiki/London,_Kiribati" title="London, Kiribati">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kiritimati" title="Kiritimati">Kiritimati</a> Island). The groups that represent <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelagoes</a> have no administrative function. They are: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands" title="Phoenix Islands">Phoenix Islands</a>, in one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_protected_areas_in_the_world" class="mw-redirect" title="List of largest protected areas in the world">largest marine protected areas</a> on Earth (was largest from 2008 to 2010)<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The original districts before independence were: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Banaba" title="Banaba">Banaba</a> (Ocean Island)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Tarawa_Atoll" class="mw-redirect" title="Tarawa Atoll">Tarawa Atoll</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Northern_Gilbert_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Gilbert Islands">Northern Gilbert Islands</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Central_Gilbert_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Gilbert Island">Central Gilbert Island</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/South_Gilbert_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="South Gilbert Islands">Southern Gilbert Islands</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Four of the former districts (including Tarawa) lie in the Gilbert Islands, where most of the country's population lives. Five of the Line Islands are uninhabited (<a href="/wiki/Malden_Island" title="Malden Island">Malden Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starbuck_Island" title="Starbuck Island">Starbuck Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Island" title="Caroline Island">Caroline Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vostok_Island" title="Vostok Island">Vostok Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flint_Island" title="Flint Island">Flint Island</a>). The Phoenix Islands are uninhabited except for <a href="/wiki/Kanton_Island" title="Kanton Island">Kanton</a>, and have no representation. Banaba itself is sparsely inhabited now. There is also a non-elected representative of the Banabans on <a href="/wiki/Rabi_Island" title="Rabi Island">Rabi Island</a> in Fiji. </p>
      <p>Each of the 21 inhabited islands<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> has its own local council that takes care of daily affairs. There is one council for each inhabited island, with two exceptions: Tarawa Atoll has three councils: <a href="/wiki/Betio" title="Betio">Betio</a> Town Council, <a href="/wiki/Teinainano_Urban_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Teinainano Urban Council">Teinainano Urban Council</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teinainano_Urban_Council" class="extiw" title="it:Teinainano Urban Council">it</a>]</span> (TUC) for the rest of <a href="/wiki/South_Tarawa" title="South Tarawa">South Tarawa</a>) and Eutan Tarawa Council (ETC) (for <a href="/wiki/North_Tarawa" title="North Tarawa">North Tarawa</a>); and <a href="/wiki/Tabiteuea" title="Tabiteuea">Tabiteuea</a> has two councils. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Kiribati" title="Geography of Kiribati">Geography of Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribati_regions_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Kiribati_regions_map.svg/220px-Kiribati_regions_map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Kiribati_regions_map.svg/330px-Kiribati_regions_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Kiribati_regions_map.svg/440px-Kiribati_regions_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1820" data-file-height="1370"></a>

          <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribati_regions_map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Kiribati and surrounding nations and territories, highlighting Kiribati's three island groups
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribati_map_LOC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kiribati_map_LOC.jpg/220px-Kiribati_map_LOC.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kiribati_map_LOC.jpg/330px-Kiribati_map_LOC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kiribati_map_LOC.jpg/440px-Kiribati_map_LOC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2399" data-file-height="1943"></a>

         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribati_map_LOC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Abaiang_top_view.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Abaiang_top_view.jpg/220px-Abaiang_top_view.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Abaiang_top_view.jpg/330px-Abaiang_top_view.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Abaiang_top_view.jpg/440px-Abaiang_top_view.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1050"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Abaiang_top_view.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Coconut palms in Abaiang
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kiribati consists of <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Kiribati" title="List of islands of Kiribati">32</a> atolls and one solitary island (<a href="/wiki/Banaba" title="Banaba">Banaba</a>), extending into the eastern and western hemispheres, as well as the northern and southern hemispheres. It is the only country that is situated within all four hemispheres. In terms with its <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">Exclusive economic zone</a>, it straddles three geographic subregions; Banaba (<a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesian</a>-<a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">Micronesian</a> area), the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a> (Micronesia) and the <a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands" title="Phoenix Islands">Phoenix Islands</a> (<a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesia</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> The groups of islands are: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Banaba" title="Banaba">Banaba</a>: an isolated island between <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a> and the Gilbert Islands</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a>: 16 atolls located some 1,500 kilometres (932&nbsp;mi) north of <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands" title="Phoenix Islands">Phoenix Islands</a>: 8 atolls and coral islands located some 1,800 kilometres (1,118&nbsp;mi) southeast of the Gilberts</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a>: 8 atolls and one reef, located about 3,300 kilometres (2,051&nbsp;mi) east of the Gilberts</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Banaba (or Ocean Island) is a <a href="/wiki/Raised_coral_atoll" title="Raised coral atoll">raised-coral island</a>. It was once a rich source of <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphates</a>, but was exhausted in mining before independence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliamsMacdonald1985_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliamsMacdonald1985-78">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEllis1935_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEllis1935-79">[78]</a></sup> The rest of the land in Kiribati consists of the sand and reef rock islets of atolls or coral islands, which rise only one or two metres above sea level. </p>
      <p>The soil is thin and <a href="/wiki/Calcareous" title="Calcareous">calcareous</a>. It has a low water-holding capacity and low organic matter and nutrient content—except for calcium, sodium, and magnesium. Banaba is one of the least suitable places for agriculture in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas20033_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas20033-80">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kiritimati" title="Kiritimati">Kiritimati</a> (Christmas Island) in the Line Islands is the world's largest atoll. Based on a 1995 realignment of the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a>, the Line Islands were the first area to enter into a new year, including year 2000. For that reason, <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Island" title="Caroline Island">Caroline Island</a> has been renamed <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Island">Millennium Island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> The majority of Kiribati, including the capital, is not first, for example New Zealand (UTC+13 in January) has an earlier new year. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Regional_Environment_Programme" title="Pacific Regional Environment Programme">Pacific Regional Environment Programme</a> (previously South Pacific Regional Environment Programme), two small uninhabited Kiribati islets, <a href="/wiki/Tebua_Tarawa" title="Tebua Tarawa">Tebua Tarawa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abanuea" title="Abanuea">Abanuea</a>, disappeared underwater in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> The United Nations <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a> predicts that sea levels will rise by about 50&nbsp;cm (20&nbsp;in) by 2100 due to <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Global warming">global warming</a> and a further rise would be inevitable. It is thus likely that within a century the nation's arable land will become subject to increased <a href="/wiki/Soil_salination" class="mw-redirect" title="Soil salination">soil salination</a> and will be largely submerged.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The exposure of Kiribati to changes in sea levels is exacerbated by the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_decadal_oscillation" title="Pacific decadal oscillation">Pacific decadal oscillation</a>, which is a climate switch phenomenon that results in changes from periods of <a href="/wiki/La_Ni%C3%B1a" title="La Niña">La Niña</a> to periods of <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o" title="El Niño">El Niño</a>. This has an effect on sea levels. For example, in 2000, there was a switch from periods of downward pressure of El Niño on sea levels to an upward pressure of La Niña on sea levels, which upward pressure causes more frequent and higher high tide levels. The <a href="/wiki/Perigean_spring_tide" title="Perigean spring tide">Perigean spring tide</a> (often called a <a href="/wiki/King_tide" title="King tide">king tide</a>) can result in seawater flooding low-lying areas of the islands of Kiribati.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Onotoa.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Onotoa.png/220px-Onotoa.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Onotoa.png/330px-Onotoa.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Onotoa.png/440px-Onotoa.png 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Onotoa.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>South of <a href="/wiki/Onotoa" title="Onotoa">Onotoa</a> Atoll
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg/220px-South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg/330px-South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg/440px-South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1569"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Tarawa_Atoll" class="mw-redirect" title="Tarawa Atoll">Tarawa Atoll</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Atolls" class="mw-redirect" title="Atolls">atolls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reef" title="Reef">reef</a> islands can respond to changes in sea-level. Paul Kench at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Auckland" title="University of Auckland">University of Auckland</a> in New Zealand and Arthur Webb at the <a href="/wiki/South_Pacific_Applied_Geoscience_Commission" title="South Pacific Applied Geoscience Commission">South Pacific Applied Geoscience Commission</a> in Fiji released a study in 2010 on the dynamic response of atolls and reef islands in the central Pacific. Kiribati was mentioned in the study, and Webb and Kench found that the three major urbanised islands in Kiribati—Betio, Bairiki and Nanikai—increased by 30% (36 hectares), 16.3% (5.8 hectares) and 12.5% (0.8 hectares), respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-WZ_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WZ-85">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Elsevier_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elsevier-86">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PSK2014_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PSK2014-87">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AWPK_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AWPK-88">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NG15_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NG15-89">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The study by Paul Kench and Arthur Webb recognises that the islands are extremely vulnerable to sea level rise, and concluded that: "This study did not measure vertical growth of the island surface nor does it suggest there is any change in the height of the islands. Since land height has not changed the vulnerability of the greater part of the land area of each island to submergence due to sea level rise is also unchanged and these low-lying atolls remain immediately and extremely vulnerable to inundation or sea water flooding."<sup id="cite_ref-Elsevier_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elsevier-86">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Climate Change in the Pacific Report of 2011 describes Kiribati as having a low risk of <a href="/wiki/Cyclones" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyclones">cyclones</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> however in March 2015 Kiribati experienced flooding and destruction of seawalls and coastal infrastructure as the result of <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Pam" title="Cyclone Pam">Cyclone Pam</a>, a Category 5 cyclone that devastated <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SBS15_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SBS15-91">[90]</a></sup> Kiribati remains exposed to the risk that cyclones can strip the low-lying islands of their vegetation and soil. </p>
      <p>Gradual sea-level rise also allows for coral <a href="/wiki/Polyp_(zoology)" title="Polyp (zoology)">polyp</a> activity to raise the atolls with the sea level. However, if the increase in sea level occurs at a rate faster than coral growth, or if polyp activity is damaged by <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">ocean acidification</a>, then the resilience of the atolls and reef islands is less certain.<sup id="cite_ref-PK14_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PK14-92">[91]</a></sup> Also, <a href="/wiki/Coral_bleaching" title="Coral bleaching">coral bleaching</a> has occurred on more than 60% of the coral reefs in the Maldives.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Kiribati_Adaptation_Program" title="Kiribati Adaptation Program">Kiribati Adaptation Program</a> (KAP), started in 2003, is a US$5.5 million initiative that was originally enacted by the national government of Kiribati with the support of the <a href="/wiki/Global_Environment_Facility" title="Global Environment Facility">Global Environment Facility</a> (GEF), the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Program" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Development Program">United Nations Development Program</a>, and the Japanese government. Australia later joined the coalition, donating US$1.5 million to the effort. The program aims to take place over six years, supporting measures that reduce Kiribati's vulnerability to the effects of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> and sea level rise by raising awareness of climate change, assessing and protecting available water resources, and managing inundation. At the start of the Adaptation Program, representatives from each of the inhabited atolls identified key climatic changes that had taken place over the past 20–40 years and proposed coping mechanisms to deal with these changes under four categories of urgency of need. The program is now focusing on the country's most vulnerable sectors in the most highly populated areas. Initiatives include improving water supply management in and around Tarawa; coastal management protection measures such as mangrove re-plantation and protection of public infrastructure; strengthening laws to reduce coastal erosion; and population settlement planning to reduce personal risks.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Line5304_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Line5304_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg/220px-Line5304_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Line5304_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg/330px-Line5304_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Line5304_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg/440px-Line5304_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Line5304_-_Flickr_-_NOAA_Photo_Library.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A tropical islet with palm fronds oriented in the direction of the prevailing winds.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kiribati has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">tropical rainforest climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Af</a>). From April to October, there are predominant northeastern winds and stable temperatures close to 30&nbsp;°C (86&nbsp;°F). From November to March, western gales bring rain. </p>
      <p>The fair season starts when <i>Ten Rimwimata</i> (<a href="/wiki/Antares" title="Antares">Antares</a>) appears in the sky after sunset, from May to November, when more gentle winds and currents and less rain. Then towards December, when <i>Nei Auti</i> (<a href="/wiki/Pleiades" title="Pleiades">Pleiades</a>) replaces Antares, the season of sudden westerly winds and more heavy rain discourages any far travel from island to island.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kiribati does not experience cyclones but effects may occasionally be experienced during cyclone seasons affecting nearby Pacific Island countries such as Fiji.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-brit_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-27">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas20033_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas20033-80">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Precipitation varies significantly between islands. For example, the annual average is 3,000&nbsp;mm (120&nbsp;in) in the north and 500&nbsp;mm (20&nbsp;in) in the south of the Gilbert Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-brit_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-27">[26]</a></sup> Most of these islands are in the dry belt of the equatorial oceanic climatic zone and experience prolonged droughts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas20033_80-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas20033-80">[79]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Kiribati" title="Wildlife of Kiribati">Wildlife of Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:AcrocephalusPistorKeulemans.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/AcrocephalusPistorKeulemans.jpg/220px-AcrocephalusPistorKeulemans.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="374" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/AcrocephalusPistorKeulemans.jpg/330px-AcrocephalusPistorKeulemans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/AcrocephalusPistorKeulemans.jpg/440px-AcrocephalusPistorKeulemans.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1915" data-file-height="3253"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:AcrocephalusPistorKeulemans.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Bokikokiko" title="Bokikokiko">bokikokiko</a> (<i>Acrocephalus aequinoctialis</i>) is the only land wildlife species endemic to Kiribati.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kiribati contains three ecosystems: <a href="/wiki/Central_Polynesian_tropical_moist_forests" title="Central Polynesian tropical moist forests">Central Polynesian tropical moist forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Micronesia_tropical_moist_forests" title="Eastern Micronesia tropical moist forests">Eastern Micronesia tropical moist forests</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Western_Polynesian_tropical_moist_forests" title="Western Polynesian tropical moist forests">Western Polynesian tropical moist forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-97">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Because of the relatively young geological age of the islands and atolls and high level of <a href="/wiki/Soil_salination" class="mw-redirect" title="Soil salination">soil salination</a>, the flora of Kiribati is somewhat unhealthy. The Gilbert Islands contain about 83 indigenous and 306 introduced plants, whereas the corresponding numbers for Line and Phoenix Islands are 67 and 283. None of these species are <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a>, and about half of the indigenous ones have a limited distribution and became endangered or nearly extinct due to human activities such as phosphate mining.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas200322_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas200322-98">[97]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Babai.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Babai.jpg/220px-Babai.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Babai.jpg/330px-Babai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Babai.jpg/440px-Babai.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Babai.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>Babai</i> or swamp taro in Butaritari
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">Coconut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pandanus_tectorius" title="Pandanus tectorius">pandanus</a> palms and <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">breadfruit</a> trees are the most common <i>wild</i> plants,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-brit_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brit-27">[26]</a></sup> whereas the five most cultivated crops but the traditional <i>Babai</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Cyrtosperma_merkusii" title="Cyrtosperma merkusii">Cyrtosperma merkusii</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> are imported <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cabbage" title="Chinese cabbage">Chinese cabbage</a>, pumpkin, tomato, watermelon and cucumber.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas200314_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas200314-101">[100]</a></sup> Over eighty per cent of the population participates in either farming or fishing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoseley2014191_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoseley2014191-102">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rotjan_-_Enderbury_Day_1_-_2nd_half_(62).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Rotjan_-_Enderbury_Day_1_-_2nd_half_%2862%29.JPG/220px-Rotjan_-_Enderbury_Day_1_-_2nd_half_%2862%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Rotjan_-_Enderbury_Day_1_-_2nd_half_%2862%29.JPG/330px-Rotjan_-_Enderbury_Day_1_-_2nd_half_%2862%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Rotjan_-_Enderbury_Day_1_-_2nd_half_%2862%29.JPG/440px-Rotjan_-_Enderbury_Day_1_-_2nd_half_%2862%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2208" data-file-height="1656"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rotjan_-_Enderbury_Day_1_-_2nd_half_(62).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Coral reefs, part of the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands_Protected_Area" title="Phoenix Islands Protected Area">Phoenix Islands Protected Area</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Seaweed_farming" title="Seaweed farming">Seaweed farming</a> is an important part of the economy<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The reason for this is unclear. (February 2017)">why?</span></a></i>]</sup>, with two major species <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eucheuma_alcarezii&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eucheuma alcarezii (page does not exist)">Eucheuma alcarezii</a></i> and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eucheuma_spinosium&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eucheuma spinosium (page does not exist)">Eucheuma spinosium</a></i> introduced to the local lagoons from the Philippines in 1977. It competes with collection of the black-lipped pearl oyster (<i><a href="/wiki/Pinctada_margaritifera" title="Pinctada margaritifera">Pinctada margaritifera</a></i>) and shellfish,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas200317_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas200317-103">[102]</a></sup> which are dominated by the strombid gastropod (<i><a href="/wiki/Strombus_luhuanus" class="mw-redirect" title="Strombus luhuanus">Strombus luhuanus</a></i>) and Anadara cockles (<i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anadara_uropigimelana&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Anadara uropigimelana (page does not exist)">Anadara uropigimelana</a></i>), whereas the stocks of the giant clam (<i><a href="/wiki/Tridacna_gigas" class="mw-redirect" title="Tridacna gigas">Tridacna gigas</a></i>) have been largely exhausted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas200317–19_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas200317–19-104">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kiribati has a few land mammals, none being indigenous or endemic. They include the Polynesian rat (<i><a href="/wiki/Rattus_exulans" class="mw-redirect" title="Rattus exulans">Rattus exulans</a></i>), dogs, cats and pigs. Among the 75 bird species, the <a href="/wiki/Bokikokiko" title="Bokikokiko">Bokikokiko</a> (<i>Acrocephalus aequinoctialis</i>) is endemic to <a href="/wiki/Kiritimati" title="Kiritimati">Kiritimati</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas200322_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas200322-98">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are 600–800 species of inshore and pelagic finfish, some 200 species of corals and about 1000 species of shellfish.<sup id="cite_ref-LPS_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LPS-105">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas200323_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas200323-106">[105]</a></sup> Fishing mostly targets the family <a href="/wiki/Scombridae" title="Scombridae">Scombridae</a>, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Skipjack_tuna" title="Skipjack tuna">skipjack tuna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yellowfin_tuna" title="Yellowfin tuna">yellowfin tuna</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Flying_fish" title="Flying fish">flying fish</a> (<i>Cypselurus</i> spp.). <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas200315_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas200315-107">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Dogs were already accompanying the first inhabitants but were re-introduced by European settlers: they have continued to grow in numbers and are roaming in traditional packs,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> particularly around South Tarawa. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Kiribati" title="Economy of Kiribati">Economy of Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribatisupermarket.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Kiribatisupermarket.jpg/220px-Kiribatisupermarket.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Kiribatisupermarket.jpg/330px-Kiribatisupermarket.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Kiribatisupermarket.jpg/440px-Kiribatisupermarket.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribatisupermarket.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Bosj's warehouse in Kiribati.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribati_Abaiang_Store.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Kiribati_Abaiang_Store.jpg/220px-Kiribati_Abaiang_Store.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Kiribati_Abaiang_Store.jpg/330px-Kiribati_Abaiang_Store.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Kiribati_Abaiang_Store.jpg/440px-Kiribati_Abaiang_Store.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="1188"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribati_Abaiang_Store.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Goods in a shop on the outer islands.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribati_Exports_Treemap_(2013).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Kiribati_Exports_Treemap_%282013%29.png/220px-Kiribati_Exports_Treemap_%282013%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Kiribati_Exports_Treemap_%282013%29.png/330px-Kiribati_Exports_Treemap_%282013%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Kiribati_Exports_Treemap_%282013%29.png/440px-Kiribati_Exports_Treemap_%282013%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1127" data-file-height="497"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribati_Exports_Treemap_(2013).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Exports of Kiribati
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kiribati has few natural resources. Commercially viable <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphate</a> deposits on <a href="/wiki/Banaba" title="Banaba">Banaba</a> were exhausted at the time of independence. <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">Copra</a> and fish now represent the bulk of production and exports. Kiribati is considered one of the <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Least developed country">least developed countries</a> in the world. </p>
      <p>In one form or another, Kiribati gets a large portion of its income from abroad. Examples include fishing licences, development assistance, workers' <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a>, especially the seafarers issued from <a href="/wiki/Marine_Training_Centre" title="Marine Training Centre">Marine Training Centre</a>, and a few tourists. Given Kiribati's limited domestic production ability, it must import nearly all of its essential foodstuffs and manufactured items; it depends on these external sources of income for financing. </p>
      <p>The economy of Kiribati benefits from international development assistance programs. The multilateral donors providing development assistance in 2009 were the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (A$9 million), the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> (A$3.7 million), UNICEF, and the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (A$100,000).<sup id="cite_ref-IMF_2011_SA_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_2011_SA-109">[108]</a></sup> The bilateral donors providing development assistance in 2009 were Australia (A$11 million), Japan (A$2 million), <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> (A$6.6 million), <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> (A$10.6 million), and other donors providing A$16.2 million, including technical assistance grants from the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IMF_2011_SA_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_2011_SA-109">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-110">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The major donors in 2010/2011 were Australia (A$15 million), Taiwan (A$11 million); New Zealand (A$6 million), the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> (A$4 million) and the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mfat_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfat-111">[110]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1956, <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands" title="Gilbert and Ellice Islands">Gilbert and Ellice Islands</a> established a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_wealth_fund" title="Sovereign wealth fund">sovereign wealth fund</a> to act as a store of wealth for the country's earnings from <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphate</a> mining. In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Revenue_Equalization_Reserve_Fund" title="Revenue Equalization Reserve Fund">Revenue Equalization Reserve Fund</a> was valued at US$400 million.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> The RERF assets declined from A$637 million (420% of GDP) in 2007 to A$570.5 million (350% of GDP) in 2009<sup id="cite_ref-IMF_2011_SA_109-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_2011_SA-109">[108]</a></sup> as the result of the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007–08">global financial crisis</a> and exposure to failed Icelandic banks. In addition, draw-downs were made by the government of Kiribati to finance budgetary shortfalls during this period.<sup id="cite_ref-IMF_2011_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_2011-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In May 2011, the IMF country report assessment of the economy of Kiribati is that "After two years of contraction, the economy recovered in the second half of 2010 and inflation pressure dissipated. It is estimated to have grown by 1.75% for the year. Despite a weather-related drop in copra production, private sector activity appears to have picked up, especially in retail. Tourist arrivals rebounded by 20% compared to 2009, although from a very low base. Despite the rise in world food and fuel prices, inflation has bounced from 2008 crisis-highs into negative territory, reflecting the strong appreciation of the Australian dollar, which is used as the domestic currency, and a decline in the world price of rice. Credit growth in the overall economy declined in 2009 as economic activity stalled. But it started to pick up in the second half of 2010 as the recovery gained traction".<sup id="cite_ref-IMF_2011_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_2011-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A major Australian bank, <a href="/wiki/Australia_and_New_Zealand_Banking_Group" title="Australia and New Zealand Banking Group">ANZ</a>, maintains a presence on Kiribati<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> with a number of branches and <a href="/wiki/Automated_teller_machine" title="Automated teller machine">ATM</a> units. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Kiribati" title="Transport in Kiribati">Transport in Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bonriki_International_Airport2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bonriki_International_Airport2.jpg/220px-Bonriki_International_Airport2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bonriki_International_Airport2.jpg/330px-Bonriki_International_Airport2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bonriki_International_Airport2.jpg/440px-Bonriki_International_Airport2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bonriki_International_Airport2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bonriki_International_Airport" title="Bonriki International Airport">Bonriki International Airport</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kiribati has had two domestic airlines: <a href="/wiki/Air_Kiribati" title="Air Kiribati">Air Kiribati</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coral_Sun_Airways" title="Coral Sun Airways">Coral Sun Airways</a>. Both airlines are based in Tarawa's <a href="/wiki/Bonriki_International_Airport" title="Bonriki International Airport">Bonriki International Airport</a> and serve destinations across the Gilbert Islands only: <a href="/wiki/Banaba" title="Banaba">Banaba</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands" title="Phoenix Islands">Phoenix Islands</a> are not served by the domestic carriers. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:A%C3%A9roport_de_Makin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/A%C3%A9roport_de_Makin.jpg/220px-A%C3%A9roport_de_Makin.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/A%C3%A9roport_de_Makin.jpg/330px-A%C3%A9roport_de_Makin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/A%C3%A9roport_de_Makin.jpg/440px-A%C3%A9roport_de_Makin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:A%C3%A9roport_de_Makin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Makin_Airport" title="Makin Airport">Makin Airfield</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Cassidy_International_Airport" title="Cassidy International Airport">Cassidy International Airport</a> on <a href="/wiki/Kiritimati" title="Kiritimati">Kiritimati</a> has an international service provided by <a href="/wiki/Fiji_Airways" title="Fiji Airways">Fiji Airways</a>: <a href="/wiki/Nadi_International_Airport" title="Nadi International Airport">Nadi</a> to Cassidy Airport and then to <a href="/wiki/Daniel_K._Inouye_International_Airport" title="Daniel K. Inouye International Airport">Honolulu</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Kiribati" title="Demographics of Kiribati">Demographics of Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Children_in_Bairiki_Square,_Tarawa,_Kiribati.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Children_in_Bairiki_Square%2C_Tarawa%2C_Kiribati.JPG/220px-Children_in_Bairiki_Square%2C_Tarawa%2C_Kiribati.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Children_in_Bairiki_Square%2C_Tarawa%2C_Kiribati.JPG/330px-Children_in_Bairiki_Square%2C_Tarawa%2C_Kiribati.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Children_in_Bairiki_Square%2C_Tarawa%2C_Kiribati.JPG/440px-Children_in_Bairiki_Square%2C_Tarawa%2C_Kiribati.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Children_in_Bairiki_Square,_Tarawa,_Kiribati.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/I-Kiribati" class="mw-redirect" title="I-Kiribati">I-Kiribati</a> children in <a href="/wiki/South_Tarawa" title="South Tarawa">South Tarawa</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The November 2015 census showed a population of 110,136. About 90% lived in the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a>, with about 50% of them on <a href="/wiki/South_Tarawa" title="South Tarawa">South Tarawa</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Betio" title="Betio">Betio</a>, the biggest township.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Until recently, people lived mostly in villages with populations between 50 and 3,000 on the outer islands. Most houses are made of materials obtained from coconut and pandanus trees. Frequent droughts and infertile soil hinder reliable large-scale agriculture, so the islanders have largely turned to the sea for livelihood and subsistence. Most are outrigger sailors and fishermen. Copra plantations serve as a second source of employment. In recent years large numbers of citizens have moved to the more urban island capital of Tarawa, where Betio is the largest town and <a href="/wiki/South_Tarawa" title="South Tarawa">South Tarawa</a> reunites larger towns like <a href="/wiki/Bikenibeu" title="Bikenibeu">Bikenibeu</a> or <a href="/wiki/Teaoraereke" title="Teaoraereke">Teaoraereke</a>. Increasing urbanisation has raised the population of South Tarawa to 63,017.<sup id="cite_ref-US_State_Dept_59-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_State_Dept-59">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IMF_2011_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_2011-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (August 2017)">page&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Landscape,_Kiribati,_2011._Photo-_Erin_Magee_-_DFAT_(12425893525).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Landscape%2C_Kiribati%2C_2011._Photo-_Erin_Magee_-_DFAT_%2812425893525%29.jpg/220px-Landscape%2C_Kiribati%2C_2011._Photo-_Erin_Magee_-_DFAT_%2812425893525%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Landscape%2C_Kiribati%2C_2011._Photo-_Erin_Magee_-_DFAT_%2812425893525%29.jpg/330px-Landscape%2C_Kiribati%2C_2011._Photo-_Erin_Magee_-_DFAT_%2812425893525%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Landscape%2C_Kiribati%2C_2011._Photo-_Erin_Magee_-_DFAT_%2812425893525%29.jpg/440px-Landscape%2C_Kiribati%2C_2011._Photo-_Erin_Magee_-_DFAT_%2812425893525%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2590" data-file-height="1726"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Landscape,_Kiribati,_2011._Photo-_Erin_Magee_-_DFAT_(12425893525).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Village on Kiribati
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">
           <th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Ethnic groups in Kiribati</th>
          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">Ethnic groups</td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">percent</td> 
          </tr>

           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">I-Kiribati</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:darkgreen; width:96.23%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">96.23%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Part I-Kiribati</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:purple; width:1.79%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1.79%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Tuvalu</td>

            <div style="background:red; width:0.18%; overflow: hidden;">

            <div style="background:black; width:1.8%; overflow: hidden;">
