        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>The native people of Kiribati are called <a href="/wiki/I-Kiribati" class="mw-redirect" title="I-Kiribati">I-Kiribati</a>. Ethnically, the I-Kiribati are <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_languages" title="Oceanic languages">Oceanians</a> but were often classified as "<a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">Micronesians</a>", an ethnicity with no scientific background.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> Recent archaeological evidence indicates that <a href="/wiki/Austronesians" class="mw-redirect" title="Austronesians">Austronesians</a> originally settled the islands thousands of years ago. Around the 14th century, Fijians, Samoans, and Tongans invaded the islands, thus diversifying the ethnic range and introducing <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_languages" title="Polynesian languages">Polynesian</a> linguistic traits. Intermarriage among all ancestral groups, however, has led to a population reasonably homogeneous in appearance and traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-US_State_Dept_59-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_State_Dept-59">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The people of Kiribati speak <a href="/wiki/Gilbertese_language" title="Gilbertese language">Gilbertese</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_languages" title="Oceanic languages">Oceanic language</a>. English is the other <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>, but is not used very often outside the island capital of <a href="/wiki/South_Tarawa" title="South Tarawa">South Tarawa</a>. It is more likely that some English is mixed in its use with Gilbertese. Older generations of I-Kiribati tend to use more complicated versions of the language. Several words in Gilbertese have been adopted from European settlers, for instance, <i>kamea</i> is one of the Gilbertese words for dog, <i>kiri</i> being the Oceanic one<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> which has its origins in the I-Kiribati people hearing the European settlers saying "come here" to their dogs, and adopting that as <i>kamea</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearns1973228_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearns1973228-117">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Many other <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanwords</a> have been adopted (like <i>buun</i>, spoon, <i>moko</i>, smoke, <i>beeki</i>, pig, <i>batoro</i>, bottle) but some typical Gilbertese words are quite common, even for European objects (like <i>wanikiba</i>, plane – the flying canoe, <i>rebwerebwe</i>, motorbike – for the motor noise, <i>kauniwae</i>, shoes – the cow for the feet). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Kiribati" title="Religion in Kiribati">Religion in Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribati(008).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Kiribati%28008%29.JPG/220px-Kiribati%28008%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Kiribati%28008%29.JPG/330px-Kiribati%28008%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Kiribati%28008%29.JPG/440px-Kiribati%28008%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kiribati(008).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Catholic Church in <a href="/wiki/Betio" title="Betio">Betio</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is the major religion in Kiribati, having been introduced by <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> in the 19th century. The population is predominantly Catholic (57.3%), with Protestant denominations (Kiribati Protestant Church, then <a href="/wiki/Kiribati_Uniting_Church" title="Kiribati Uniting Church">Kiribati Uniting Church</a>) accounting for 31.3%. <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> (5.3%), <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith_in_Kiribati" title="Baháʼí Faith in Kiribati">Baháʼí Faith</a> (2.1%), <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a> (1.9%), Pentecostals, Jehovah's Witnesses, and others small faiths account all for less than 10% (2015 census). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Oceania#Kiribati" class="mw-redirect" title="List of hospitals in Oceania">List of hospitals in Oceania §&nbsp;Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a> where 90% of Kiribati population is living, boasts some of the highest population densities in the Pacific, rivaling, without any tall building, cities like <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> or <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>. This overcrowding provokes a great amount of pollution, worsening the quality and length of life. Due to insufficient sanitation and water filtration systems, worsened by the fragility of the <a href="/wiki/Lens_(hydrology)" title="Lens (hydrology)">water lens</a> of the atolls and by Climate Change, only about 66% have access to clean water. Waterborne diseases grow at record levels throughout the islands. Poor sanitation has led to an increase in cases of conjunctivitis, diarrhea, dysentery, and fungal infections. Around 60% of adults smoke tobacco products on a regular basis, the highest proportion in the world. Due to this and other lifestyle diseases, such as diabetes, there has been a drastic spike in amputations on the islands, doubling in a few years. </p>
      <p>As a consequence, the population of Kiribati has a quite low life expectancy at birth of 68.46 years,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> even if this data is of only 66.9 years, provided elsewhere – Kiribati ranks last in life expectancy out of the 20 nations of Oceania. This life expectancy is 64.3 for males, and 69.5 for females and there is an infant mortality rate of 41 deaths per 1,000 live births.<sup id="cite_ref-IMF_2011_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_2011-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">Tuberculosis</a> has a small presence in the country, with 365 cases per 100,000 a year.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> Government expenditure on health was at US$268 per capita (PPP) in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> In 1990–2007, there were 23 physicians per 100,000 persons.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> Since the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuban</a> doctors in 2006, the infant mortality rate has decreased significantly.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most health problems are related to consumption of semi-raw seafood, limited food storage facilities, and bacterial contamination of fresh water supplies. In the early 2000s, between 1 and 7% of the population, depending on the island, were annually treated for food poisoning in a hospital. Modernization and cross-cultural exchange of the late 20th century brought new issues of unhealthy diet and lifestyle, heavy smoking, especially among the young, and external infections, including HIV/AIDS.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas20038–9_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas20038–9-123">[122]</a></sup> Kiribati is the country with the third highest prevalence of smoking, with 54% of the population reported as smokers.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Fresh water remains a concern of Kiribati – during the dry season (Aumaiaki), water has been drilled for instead of using rain water tanks. In recent years, there has been a longer than usual Aumaikai season resulting in additional water having to be drilled from beneath the water table. This has introduced water-borne illnesses, compounding the health problems within Kiribati.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Kiribati" title="Education in Kiribati">Education in Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_South_Pacific,_Kiribati_Campus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/University_of_South_Pacific%2C_Kiribati_Campus.jpg/220px-University_of_South_Pacific%2C_Kiribati_Campus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/University_of_South_Pacific%2C_Kiribati_Campus.jpg/330px-University_of_South_Pacific%2C_Kiribati_Campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/University_of_South_Pacific%2C_Kiribati_Campus.jpg/440px-University_of_South_Pacific%2C_Kiribati_Campus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="1584"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_South_Pacific,_Kiribati_Campus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_South_Pacific" title="University of the South Pacific">University of the South Pacific</a>, Kiribati Campus
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Primary education is free and compulsory for the first six years, now being extended to nine years (from 6 to 14 years). Mission schools are slowly being absorbed into the government primary school system. Higher education is expanding; students may seek technical, teacher or marine training, or study in other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-US_State_Dept_59-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_State_Dept-59">[58]</a></sup> Most choosing to do the latter have gone to Fiji to attend the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_South_Pacific" title="University of the South Pacific">University of the South Pacific</a>, and those wishing to complete medical training have been sent to Australia, New Zealand or Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The education system is organized as follows: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>preschool for childhood from 1 to 6 years;</li> 
       <li>Junior secondary school (Form 1 to 3) from 7 to 9;</li> 
       <li>Senior secondary school (Form 4 to 7) from 10 to 13.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kiribati_Ministry_of_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="Kiribati Ministry of Education">Kiribati Ministry of Education</a> is the educationy ministry. The government high schools are <a href="/wiki/King_George_V_and_Elaine_Bernacchi_School" title="King George V and Elaine Bernacchi School">King George V and Elaine Bernacchi School</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tabiteuea_North_Senior_Secondary_School&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tabiteuea North Senior Secondary School (page does not exist)">Tabiteuea North Senior Secondary School</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Melaengi_Tabai_Secondary_School&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Melaengi Tabai Secondary School (page does not exist)">Melaengi Tabai Secondary School</a>. 13 high schools are operated by Christian churches.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The University of the South Pacific has a campus in <a href="/wiki/Teaoraereke" title="Teaoraereke">Teaoraereke</a> for distant/flexible learning, but also to provide preparatory studies towards obtaining certificates, diplomas and degrees at other campus sites. </p>
      <p>The other prominent schools in Kiribati are: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Training_Centre" title="Marine Training Centre">Marine Training Centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Betio" title="Betio">Betio</a>;</li> 
       <li>the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati_Institute_of_Technology&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kiribati Institute of Technology (page does not exist)">Kiribati Institute of Technology</a>;</li> 
       <li>the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati_Fisheries_Training_Centre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kiribati Fisheries Training Centre (page does not exist)">Fisheries Training Centre</a>;</li> 
       <li>the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati_School_of_Nursing&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kiribati School of Nursing (page does not exist)">Kiribati School of Nursing</a>;</li> 
       <li>the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati_Police_Academy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kiribati Police Academy (page does not exist)">Kiribati Police Academy</a>;</li> 
       <li>the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati_Teachers_College&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kiribati Teachers College (page does not exist)">Kiribati Teachers College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Kiribati" title="Culture of Kiribati">Culture of Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Songs (<i>te anene</i>) and above all, dances (<i>te mwaie</i>), are held in high regard. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Kiribati" title="Music of Kiribati">Music of Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kiribati folk music is generally based on <a href="/wiki/Chanting" class="mw-redirect" title="Chanting">chanting</a> or other forms of vocalising, accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Body_percussion" title="Body percussion">body percussion</a>. Public performances in modern Kiribati are generally performed by a seated chorus, accompanied by a guitar. However, during formal performances of the standing dance (<i>Te Kaimatoa</i>) or the hip dance (<i>Te Buki</i>), a wooden box is used as a percussion instrument. This box is constructed to give a hollow and reverberating tone when struck simultaneously by a chorus of men sitting around it. Traditional songs are often love-themed, but there are also competitive, religious, children's, patriotic, war and wedding songs. There are also <a href="/wiki/Tirere" class="mw-redirect" title="Tirere">stick dances</a> which accompany legends and semi-historical stories.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-129">[128]</a></sup> These stick dances or "tirere" (pronounced seerere) are performed only during major festivals. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dance">Dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dance_in_Kiribati" title="Dance in Kiribati">Dance in Kiribati</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bonriki_International_Airport_welcome.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bonriki_International_Airport_welcome.jpg/220px-Bonriki_International_Airport_welcome.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bonriki_International_Airport_welcome.jpg/330px-Bonriki_International_Airport_welcome.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bonriki_International_Airport_welcome.jpg/440px-Bonriki_International_Airport_welcome.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bonriki_International_Airport_welcome.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A welcome display.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The uniqueness of Kiribati when compared with other forms of Pacific island dance is its emphasis on the outstretched arms of the dancer and the sudden birdlike movement of the head. The <a href="/wiki/Great_frigatebird" title="Great frigatebird">Frigate bird</a> (<i>Fregata minor</i>) on the Kiribati flag refers to this bird-like style of Kiribati dancing. Most dances are in the standing or sitting position with movement limited and staggered. Smiling whilst dancing is generally considered vulgar within the context of Kiribati dancing. This is due to its origin of not being solely as a form of entertainment but as a form of storytelling and a display of the skill, beauty and endurance of the dancer.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStevenson1896_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStevenson1896-130">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhincupWhincup2001_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhincupWhincup2001-131">[130]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dance_ornament_of_conus_shell_and_pandanus_leaf_string,_Kiribati,_1891_-_Staatlichen_Museums_f%C3%BCr_V%C3%B6lkerkunde_M%C3%BCnchen_-_DSC08292.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Dance_ornament_of_conus_shell_and_pandanus_leaf_string%2C_Kiribati%2C_1891_-_Staatlichen_Museums_f%C3%BCr_V%C3%B6lkerkunde_M%C3%BCnchen_-_DSC08292.JPG/220px-Dance_ornament_of_conus_shell_and_pandanus_leaf_string%2C_Kiribati%2C_1891_-_Staatlichen_Museums_f%C3%BCr_V%C3%B6lkerkunde_M%C3%BCnchen_-_DSC08292.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Dance_ornament_of_conus_shell_and_pandanus_leaf_string%2C_Kiribati%2C_1891_-_Staatlichen_Museums_f%C3%BCr_V%C3%B6lkerkunde_M%C3%BCnchen_-_DSC08292.JPG/330px-Dance_ornament_of_conus_shell_and_pandanus_leaf_string%2C_Kiribati%2C_1891_-_Staatlichen_Museums_f%C3%BCr_V%C3%B6lkerkunde_M%C3%BCnchen_-_DSC08292.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Dance_ornament_of_conus_shell_and_pandanus_leaf_string%2C_Kiribati%2C_1891_-_Staatlichen_Museums_f%C3%BCr_V%C3%B6lkerkunde_M%C3%BCnchen_-_DSC08292.JPG/440px-Dance_ornament_of_conus_shell_and_pandanus_leaf_string%2C_Kiribati%2C_1891_-_Staatlichen_Museums_f%C3%BCr_V%C3%B6lkerkunde_M%C3%BCnchen_-_DSC08292.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dance_ornament_of_conus_shell_and_pandanus_leaf_string,_Kiribati,_1891_-_Staatlichen_Museums_f%C3%BCr_V%C3%B6lkerkunde_M%C3%BCnchen_-_DSC08292.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Dance ornament of 1891
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Traditionally, the staple diet of the I-Kiribati was the abundance of seafood and coconuts. Starch based carbohydrate sources were not plentiful due to the hostile climate of the atolls with only the northernmost atolls being viable for constant agriculture. The national crop <i><a href="/wiki/Cyrtosperma_merkusii" title="Cyrtosperma merkusii">bwabwai</a></i> was only eaten during special celebrations along with pork. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Babai.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Babai.jpg/220px-Babai.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Babai.jpg/330px-Babai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Babai.jpg/440px-Babai.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Babai.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bwabwai cultivation in <a href="/wiki/Butaritari" title="Butaritari">Butaritari</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>To complement the rather low consumption of carbohydrates in their diets, the I-Kiribati processed the sap and fruit of the abundant Pandanus and Coconut trees into different beverages and foods such as <i>te karewe</i> (fresh daily sap of the coconut tree) or <i>te tuae</i> (dried pandanus cake) and <i>te kabubu</i> (dried pandanus flour) from pandanus fruit pulp and <i>te kamaimai</i> (coconut sap syrup) from coconut sap. </p>
      <p>After World War II, rice became a daily staple in most households which is still the case today. Majority of seafood, fish in particular is eaten sashimi style with either coconut sap, soy sauce or vinegar based dressings in use often combined with chillies and onions. </p>
      <p>Coconut crabs and mud crabs is traditionally given to breastfeeding mothers, with the belief that it stimulated the production of good quality breastmilk. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Kiribati_at_the_Olympics" title="Kiribati at the Olympics">Kiribati at the Olympics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kiribati_at_the_2014_Commonwealth_Games" title="Kiribati at the 2014 Commonwealth Games">Kiribati at the 2014 Commonwealth Games</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bairiki_National_Stadium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Bairiki_National_Stadium.jpg/220px-Bairiki_National_Stadium.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Bairiki_National_Stadium.jpg/330px-Bairiki_National_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/71/Bairiki_National_Stadium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="406" data-file-height="226"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bairiki_National_Stadium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bairiki National Stadium, at Bairiki, Tarawa
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kiribati has competed at the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> since <a href="/wiki/1998_Commonwealth_Games" title="1998 Commonwealth Games">1998</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> since <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004</a>. It sent three competitors to its first Olympics, two sprinters and a weightlifter.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> Kiribati won its first ever Commonwealth Games medal at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Commonwealth_Games" title="2014 Commonwealth Games">2014 Commonwealth Games</a> when weightlifter <a href="/wiki/David_Katoatau" title="David Katoatau">David Katoatau</a> won Gold in the 105&nbsp;kg Group.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport. <a href="/wiki/Kiribati_Islands_Football_Federation" title="Kiribati Islands Football Federation">Kiribati Islands Football Federation</a> (KIFF) is an associate member of the <a href="/wiki/Oceania_Football_Confederation" title="Oceania Football Confederation">Oceania Football Confederation</a>, but not of world-governing body <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kiribati_national_football_team" title="Kiribati national football team">Kiribati National team</a> has played ten matches, all of which it has lost, and all at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_Pacific_Games" title="Football at the Pacific Games">Pacific Games</a> from 1979 to 2011. The Kiribati football stadium is <a href="/wiki/Bairiki_National_Stadium" title="Bairiki National Stadium">Bairiki National Stadium</a>, which has a capacity of 2,500.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Betio_Soccer_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Betio Soccer Field (page does not exist)">Betio Soccer Field</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Betio_Soccer_Field" class="extiw" title="pl:Betio Soccer Field">pl</a>]</span> is home to a number of local sporting teams.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Outside_perspectives">Outside perspectives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Outside perspectives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Edward_Carlyon_Eliot" title="Edward Carlyon Eliot">Edward Carlyon Eliot</a>, who was Resident Commissioner of the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands" title="Gilbert and Ellice Islands">Gilbert and Ellice Islands</a> (now Kiribati &amp; Tuvalu) from 1913 to 1920 describes this period in his book <i>Broken Atoms</i> (autobiographical reminiscences) Pub. G. Bles, London, 1938. </p>
      <p>Sir <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Grimble" title="Arthur Grimble">Arthur Grimble</a> wrote about his time working in the British colonial service in Kiribati (then the Gilbert Islands) from 1914 to 1932 in two popular books <i>A Pattern of Islands</i> (1952)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrimble1952_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrimble1952-42">[41]</a></sup> and <i>Return to the Islands</i> (1957). He also undertook academic studies of Gilbertese culture. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/John_Hilary_Smith" title="John Hilary Smith">John Smith</a>, the last governor of the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands" title="Gilbert and Ellice Islands">Gilbert and Ellice Islands</a> wrote his memoir <i>An Island in the Autumn</i> (2011).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2011_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2011-136">[135]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/J._Maarten_Troost" title="J. Maarten Troost">J. Maarten Troost</a>'s more recent autobiographical experiences in <a href="/wiki/Tarawa" title="Tarawa">Tarawa</a> are documented in his book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sex_Lives_of_Cannibals" title="The Sex Lives of Cannibals">The Sex Lives of Cannibals</a></i> (2004).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETroost2004_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETroost2004-137">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Alice Piciocchi's illustrated essay, <i>Kiribati. Cronache illustrate da una terra (s)perduta</i>, (2016) Milan: 24 ORE Cultura, also translated into French (2018, éditions du Rouergue), tries to write and portray a comprehensive encyclopedic book of nowadays Kiribati.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiribati&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

        <li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrimble1952-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrimble1952_42-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrimble1952_42-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFGrimble1952">Grimble 1952</a>.</span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">That treaty was signed shortly after independence and ratified in 1983, the United States relinquishing all claims to the sparsely-inhabited Phoenix Islands, and those of the Line Islands that are part of Kiribati territory.</span> </li>

        <li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Kiribati was then granted sovereignty on <a href="/wiki/Canton_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Canton Island">Canton Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enderbury_Island" title="Enderbury Island">Enderbury Island</a>, Birnie Island, Mckean Island, Rawaki, Manra, Orona, and Nikumaroro from the Phoenix Islands; and <a href="/wiki/Teraina" title="Teraina">Teraina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tabuaeran" title="Tabuaeran">Tabuaeran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kiritimati" title="Kiritimati">Kiritimati</a>, Malden Island, Starbuck Island, Caroline Islands, Vostok Islands and Flint Island from the Line Islands.</span> </li>

          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mfed.gov.ki/statistics/documents/2015_Population_Census_Report_Volume_1final_211016.pdf">"2015 Population and Housing Census, Volume 1: Management Report and Basic Tables"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>.
